Column 9:  This column is very badly damaged, and little of certainty can be recovered because of the 
advanced disintegration of its script.  The only preserved portions are those segments attached to the 
upper right and left margins, adjoining the columns on either side.  The best photo for most of the 
preserved text is IMneg. 3839, which has picked up the ink remains quite well.  There appear to be 37 
(rather than 36) lines in this column, based on a count along the fully preserved left margin. 
9.3: ̇ נ ̇ד ̇ א̇ נטל ̇ ח ̇ ה ]  The word ̇ א̇ נטל ̇ ח seems to be a form of the noun אטלח “final decision, irredeemable 
sentence.” (cf. Jastrow I, p. 467). 
Column 10:  Portions of each margin are preserved for col. 10, although the center is in various stages of 
disintegration.  A new sheet of parchment begins here, with the joint seam and scribal dots (to indicate 
where the manuscript preparer should inscribe lines) clearly seen in all photographs.  The standard 
length of the columns on this sheet is 35 lines, and there is a very crudely written tsade (indeed, I 
continue to question whether it is a tsade) in the upper, righthand corner of the sheet (cf. cols. 5 and 17). 
10.1: אבר GMT/AW/B3 ]  MQS/F הבר.  The aleph is clear on BZ10T. 
10.1: ֯כ֯ר̇ב ] ת [ ֯ מל ֯ר ֯ ה ]  MQS/F/AW ̇ב ◌◌ ל ◌ ת ; B3 אלוב ֯ מ לטב.  There are at least three letters between the bet and

10.1: ינ ̇ מ B3 ]  MQS/GMT/F/AW ינ ̇ב.  The left, upper part of the mem is quite clear on IMneg. x 86-4451.

10.2: ̇ ו ֯ נל ח ◌◌ ֯ א ◌◌ ל ̇ ן ֯ יל ֯ מ ֯ ו ֯כ ל ֯ ו ֯ ה ] ן ]  MQS/F/AW ̇ נל ̇ ו ח ◌◌ ̇ ל֯ב ̇יל֯ י ̇א ◌◌ ; B3 הו ֯ הל הב אילילב ] .  While my reading is far

horizontal stroke is readily apparent in this position (i.e. a mem, or similar letter).  Finally, it is clear that 
there is a word break between the nun of my ̇ ן ֯ יל ֯ מ and the following letter.  Following this phrase there 
appears to be a short segment of text (3-4 letters) which has been effaced. 
10.3: ֯ א֯ יל֯ יל̇ב MQS/F/AW/B3 ]  I follow the reading first offered by MQS with reservation.  There appears to 
be too much space between the lameds for a yod alone, but BZ10T is very difficult to read here.  
Additionally, the lameds of אילילב in 20.12 are also spaced farther apart than one might expect. 
10.8:  ֯ י ֯ר ̇ א̇ ו ◌◌ ך֯ י ֯ א̇י ̇רב ]  MQS/F/AW ◌◌◌ ◌◌◌ ̇א֯כ̇רב ̇ך ; B3 וכרמ ןור֯כ֯ ד ֯ תי ] ן .  The transcription of B3 may be safely

Column 11:  Col. 11 is attached to col. 12, and in similar condition (see below). 
11.1: ת֯ י ֯ ו ֯ ה MQS/GMT/F/AW ]  B3 תיז ֯ ח.  Either reading is possible based on the scant ink remains, but the

11.1: ת ̇ י ̇ א ̇ תוב ]  The superscripted yod appears to be in a different scribal hand than the surrounding script, 
having a much larger head than is typical. 
11.1: ̇ר ֯ א֯ב ̇י ̇ א MQS/AW ]  F ̇ב ̇ א ̇י ̇ר א ;  וראו לא ] .  The reading of MQS/AW is preferable to F, since the letters א̇י ̇ר

11.9: אי ֯רבדמדו MQS/AW ]  F/B3 ̇רבדמו אי .  The dalet is clear in BZ11T. 
11.9: ̇ב֯ ו ֯ על ̇ר אי F ]  MQS/AW על ◌ רב אי ; B3 אירבעמל.  I follow F with hesitation, since the first few letters are 
very difficult to read on the photographs.  F translated the word as “thickets,” taking it to be related to 
the feminine noun הרבוע (“branch, sprout”).  This strikes me as unlikely, especially since the Aramaic 
words רבוע (“transient, passerby”) and רביע (“traveler, border, side”) might lend themselves geographic 
extrapolations, such as my “intermediate regions” or some similar term (perhaps “plains”).  B3’s 
transcription is not impossible, nor אירברבל (which may be materially best).  In any case, this appears to 
be another topographic reference of some sort. 
11.13: ̇ד ֯ מ֯ ע ]  MQS/AW ֯ ע ֯ב ̇ד ; F ̇ ע ̇ב ̇ר .  MQS/AW’s reading of the dalet looks correct (contra F), while the

11.14: ̇ ל ̇ר֯ב֯ ג ̇י ֯ד ֯ צ ̇ ק א MQS/F/AW ]  B3 ל ֯ד֯ב ֯ ע אקדצ .  The first word is too disintergrated to read with certainty.

11.15: ֯ יל ◌◌◌◌ ̇ מ ֯ ן ̇ ש ̇ מ ̇י ̇ א ]  MQS/AW ֯ יל ◌◌ ◌◌ ◌ ̇ ש ̇ מ ̇י ̇ א ; F ̇יל ] הרמ [ ̇ ש ̇ מ ̇י ̇ א ; B3 ֯ א ֯ הל ֯ א ֯ י ֯ד ןמ אימש .  There is too 
much space between ֯ יל and ̇ א̇י ̇ מ ̇ ש (approximately 6 letters, depending on which they are) for F’s 
reconstruction to be correct.  The words אשידק and אריע (cf. 6.13) seem equally implausible in this gap 
and would not be expectd based on other usage of divine titles.  A possible mem stands before the word 
̇ א̇י ̇ מ ̇ ש, but there is not enough room following it for both a resh and a heh.  I have taken the following, 
faint, vertical stroke as a final nun (so also B3), although this is far from certain.  This ןמ would make an 
intervening הרמ more plausible.  AW curiously follows F’s translation, but not his transcription.

11.18: ל ◌◌◌ ]  Perhaps ל חונ , as the second letter has the bottom portion of nun, bet, kaph or peh.  Certainly not

11.19: ◌◌ ̇ ש֯ב ןינ ]  MQS/F/AW ] יד [ י ןינש .  In BZ11BM there appears to be a horizontal top stroke before the

Column 12:  Here begins the column first published by Greenfield and Qimron (hence the switch from MQS 
to GQ).  The left central portion is its best preserved part, with much of the surrounding area being 
severely disintegrated.  The BZ photographs are glossy, and are at times difficult to read. 
12.1: ] י ןנעב [ ֯ ת֯ב ֯ ה ]  There does not appear to be room for all the letters suggested by GQ, nor is there any 
evidence of a final nun, even though the leather where it should be is in-tact.  I follow their proposal 
with hearty reservation, although the general import is, no doubt, correct. 
12.1: אננעב GQ/B2/3/F ]  GMT/AW ננעב ה .  The aleph is certain. 
12.1:  ̇ ה̇ ו ֯ המל̇ ו ◌◌◌ ̇ תא GQ/F/AW ]  B3 תא֯ ו ֯ ה הז ֯ חמלו.  Either reading is possible for the first word, with the 
crucial fourth letter being badly damaged.  A horizontal crack runs through the final word, but there 
appear to be more than two letters preceding the aleph. 
12.3: ֯ ו ◌ ̇ עב ]  GQ/F ◌ ̇ב ̇ ש .  There seems to be space for at least two letters at the beginning of this word.  The 
left downstroke of the ayin can be faintly seen, while a full shin would nearly overlap the following aleph. 
12.7: ֯ י ֯ר֯ ו ֯ ט֯ב GQ ]  F ̇ב ̇ ט ̇ ו ̇ר ̇י ] טררוה [ .  There is not sufficient room for טררוה to be reconstructed at the end of 
this line. 
 150 
12.8: ◌◌◌ GMT/AW ]  GQ/F ם֯ר ֯כ ֯ ת; B2/3 [ ם.  The leather has a wide, horizontal split in it, and the 
penultimate kaph/nun, along with a following letter (resh/dalet?) are easily mistaken for a final mem.  In 
BZ12T the letters preceding this are unreadable.  The mention of a vineyard (םרכ) here would be odd, 
given its introduction in line 13. 
12.8: ינבו ̇ נ א ]  GQ/B2/3/GMT/F/AW ינבו ֯ י ֯ נ ֯ב .  The aleph is clear on BZ12T and IMneg. 3841, ruling out the 
reading of GQ et al.  While the top of the penultimate letter is slightly obscured in the photos, it is 
almost surely a nun, or less likely a kaph.  The 2 m. sg. ending (אכ-) is grammatically acceptable, but 
makes little sense in this context.  I have read the letter as a nun, thus representing a 1 pl. perf. form of 
the verb ינב “we built” (for other examples of this form cf. 12.16) – a reference to the more widespread 
tradition that Noah and his sons built cities after leaving the ark (cf. Jub. 7:14-17, 35; 4Q244 frg. 8). 
12.9: ל ] ינב ינבו [ ֯ ן ]  בו [ ̇ נ ̇ ן ]  GQ ל ] י ב ינ [ ֯ ן ] ◌◌◌ ב [ ןנ ; GMT/AW [ ל ] ◌◌◌ ב [ ןנ ; Bern ל ] ןוה ... ; B2/3/F ל ] ינב ב ינ [ ֯ ן ] בו [ ןנ .  
This area is badly damaged and any reconstruction is speculative.  The suggestion of GMT/AW can be 
ruled out based on available space (at least 8-9 letters between the lamed and the final bracket), while the 
reconstruction of GQ makes little sense at this point in the narrative (Noah begets his sons and 
daughters already in col. 6!).  B2/3/F’s proposal is attractive, and is essentially followed here, although the 
spacing for this phrase does not seem quite right (perhaps due to distortion of the leather).  The phrase 
ןבקנ ןנב, commonly employed in the scroll, is not possible based on space and remains.  Bernstein’s 
suggestion (p. 41) is based on a mistaken reading at the end of the previous line (cf. previous note), and 
is therefore doubtful. 
12.14: ֯ א֯ י ֯ ג ֯ ש ̇כ֯ ו ̇ ו ל ֯ ח ֯ א֯ר ֯ מ ̇ א ֯ י תת ]  GQ/GMT/AW ◌◌◌◌ ̇כ ̇ ו ל ◌◌◌◌◌◌ ֯ א ̇ ת ת ; B2/3 ֯ י ֯ ג ֯ ש לוכו ֯ א֯ר ֯ מ ֯ ח ֯ ח ֯ א תת ; F ̇ ש ̇ ג ̇י ̇א ̇ ו ̇כ ̇ ו ל 
̇ ח ̇ מ ̇ר ̇ א ̇ א ̇ ח תת .  In general, the reading first offered by B2 fits the slight ink remains quite well.  F’s 
addition of an aleph at the end of איגש is speculative, since the very beginning of the line is gone.  It is 
kept here only because it better fits the conventional grammar of the scroll.  B2/3/F’s חא תת is unlikely 
based on available space and ink remains, although there may be one vertical stroke between the aleph 
and upper right corner of the penultimate tav (there is a tear in the leather here) – perhaps a yod.  This 
word should probably be read as an aphel 1 sg. perf. form of יתא. 
12.15: ] אימדק [ Kis/B2/3/F ]  GQ ] איעיבש [ .  The reconstruction is based on Jub 7:2 (cf. F, p. 161-62 for 
discussion).  GQ base their reconstruction on Jub 7.1 instead. 
12.15: ימרכ וגבו ]  GQ/B2/3/GMT/F/AW ֯ י ֯ד ̇כ ̇ר ימ .  The word וגבו (as well as the preceding ימרכב) are clearly 
visible on BZ12M, but blurred beyond recognition in the IMneg. photos. 
12.15: ̇ימח ̇ ש ̇י ̇ א ̇ ת א ]  AY (21/חי)/GQ/B2/3/GMT/F/AW ̇ימח ̇ ש ̇י ̇ ת א .  There would have to be at least 8 letters in 
this word if it includes two yods.  The aleph preceding the tav is clear on BZ12M, and mirrors the 
morphology of י/אנאינת in 10.14 and 21.1. 
12.16: ] יד הבצנ רתב [ ̇כ ̇ א ̇ מ̇ר ]  GQ ] ימרכ יד [ ◌ ◌◌◌ ; B2/3/F ] רתב במ [ ל֯ ו ֯ א .  The letter remains do not support the 
suggestion of B2/3/F.  Most conspicuously absent is the lamed.  The occurrence of ̇א ̇ מ̇ר̇כ here (best seen 
in BZ12M) also disproves GQ’s reconstruction. 
12.16: אדחכ GQ et al. ]  AY (21/חי) אדחב.  The first letter plainly has the lower bend of a caph, not the join of 
a bet.  The same expression (with caph) is found at 21.21, 25; 22.1. 
12.16: אנלזאו GQ et al. ]  AY (21/חי) לזאו הנ .  There is no doubt that the word ends with an aleph, as is typical 
of this verbal form in the scroll. 
12.17: ]    חבדמ [ א ]  GQ ] רתאל חבדמ א [ ◌◌ א ; B2/3 ] ל בדמ ח הרמ [ אימ ֯ ש ; F ] רתאל חבדמ [ א .  None of the 
previously proposed reconstructions is satisfying.  First, there is far too much space for any of them to 
fit as proposed – somewhere between 15 and 20 letters.  Furthermore, there is no trace of the top of a 
lamed, as reconstructed by GQ/B2/3/F.  I find no evidence for B2/3’s אימ ֯ ש.  My own suggestion is 
speculation based on narrative context. 
12.18: ודח ̇ א יתובא ]  GQ/F א ̇ הוב י ̇י ֯ ת ̇ ש ̇ו .  The base stroke of the left leg of the tav, as well as the letter 
combination het-dalet-vav of ודח ̇ א, are plain on BZ12M. 
12.19: ̇ ט ֯ ש֯ ק֯ב ̇י ̇כשו ̇ב ת ֯ לע ̇ש֯ מ ̇כ יב ]  GQ/F ◌◌ ֯ י ֯ נ שו ̇ פ כ ת ֯ לע ◌◌◌ יב .  The first word is uncertain, although the tet is 
quite clear.  Only the vertical stroke of the qoph, read by GQ/F as a final nun, remains.  There does not 
 151 
appear to be room for a vav (i.e. full orthography) between the qoph and shin.  Alternatively, it may read 
̇י ̇ ט ֯ ש ̇ ן ֯ מ, which would have to mean either “my folly” or “my drinking” (spelled with a tet rather than the 
typical tav), but this seems less likely.  Remains of the upper, horizontal stroke of a kaph are faintly 
visible in ̇כשו ת̇ב , as well as the tops of shin and kaph in יב̇כ ̇ ש֯ מ. 
12.27: ̇ ה֯ נש ל֯ב ◌ ]  GQ/F ̇ ה֯ נש ̇ו ל ◌ .  The bottom stroke of a letter other than yod can be distinguished preceding 
the lamed in BZ12B. 
Column 13:  Most of the right margin of this column is shared with the left side of col. 12, forming one, large 
leaf of parchment.  Large portions of the upper and lower sections of the column are completely eaten 
away, leaving us to wonder about the full content of Noah’s dream.  In addition to the BZ photographs, 
IMneg. x 86-4449 is especially useful. 
13.8: ̇ א ̇ מד ̇ א ]  B3 אערא.  The right horn of the dalet and base stroke of the mem are plainly seen on BZ13T. 
13.8: ̇ ל ֯ ה ̇י ֯כ ̇ ן ]  MQS/AW ֯ ח ל ֯ ו ֯ פ ̇ ן ; F/B3 ̇ ח ל ̇ פ ̇י ̇ ן .  The reading is very uncertain, but the peh of MQS/AW/F does not 
appear correct based on the fragmentary top of the letter. 
13.11: ץרש אערא ץרשו GMT/B3 ]  MQS/F/AW ̇ ש ̇ר ןי אערא ןירשו .  The small, right strokes of the final tsades 
are quite plain on IMneg. 3843, solving the interpretive conundrum of F. 
13.11-12: ף ֯ ס֯ ו / א̇י ֯ מ MQS/GMT/F/AW ]  B3 ףאו / הדע .  The first two letters of the first word are almost entirely 
missing on the photographs, but the two legs expected of the lower portion of an aleph are absent.  א̇י ֯ מ 
is more certain, with the left side of the mem and the full yod visible on IMneg. 3843. 
13.13: המורב M (margin)/B3/AW ]  MQS/GMT/F אמורב.  The heh is clear on BZ13TM and IMneg. 3843. 
13.13: ̇בב ̇ ע ֯ י ̇ ע נ ןאיפ ]  MQS ̇ב ̇ ז ̇ ו ̇י ̇ ע ̇ ו ןאיפ ; GMT בועב ע ו ןאיפ ; F ̇ב ̇ ז ̇י ̇ ו ̇ ע ̇ ו ןאיפ ; B3 ירפא ןאיפוע , AW ̇ב יזז ̇ ע ו ןאיפ .  This 
phrase has obviously puzzled commentators, although much may be gained by a careful study of the 
infrared photographs.  The initial bet is abundantly clear on BZ13TM and IMneg. 3834, as is the base 
stroke of another bet following it.  A full ayin may be discerned in the next position, the sloping lower 
line of which renders all previous proposals very unlikely.  An obscured (but small) letter finishes the 
word, likely a yod, making it probable that here we have an infinitive construct (acting nominally) of 
עוב/יעב “a bursting forth.”  This makes good sense in the present context.  The first letters of the next 
word are somewhat obscured, but the top of the second letter does not resemble a typical vav/yod, and a 
bottom stroke is visible running into the base of the following peh (cf. especially IMneg. 3834).  The 
word ןאיפנע “branches” also fits the context well (for use of this same root cf. line 16). 
13.14: ̇ נ ̇ א ] אב [ ̇יפ ̇שו ברב֯ר ר ]  MQS/AW ̇ נ ̇ א ◌◌◌ ̇בב̇ר̇ב ◌◌◌◌ ̇ר ; GMT … א נ ] ב [ ברב ןי ; F ̇ נ ̇ א ] ןב [ ̇בב̇ר̇ב ◌◌◌◌ ר ; B3 
מ֯ ו ] ת [ ריפ ֯ שו ברבר .  Every letter of the word ריפשו, except the yod, is clear in BZ13TM.  The letters ברב of 
my ברב֯ר are starkly visible in IMneg. 3834, although the area preceding these letters is mostly missing.  
F’s reconstruction of ןבנא works with the available space, despite the spacing proposed by MQS and B3 
(the former with too much and the latter with too little).  ברבר is known as an alternate form of the 
adjective בר, but is often used as an itpael verbal form (so B3), which should not be absolutely ruled out 
here. 
13.15: ̇ ש֯ ו ̇ד ̇י ̇ א ן ]  MQS/F/AW ◌◌◌ ̇י ̇ א ̇ ן ; B3 ןי ֯כו ֯ ש֯ ו.  Significantly more text is preserved on IMneg. x 86-4449 than 
on the other available photographs, although the ink is somewhat blurred.  The final letters of 
MQS/F/AW appear to be correct there, while the vav-kaph combination of B3 may be confidently ruled 
out.  The meaning of this word is not entirely clear, although it may reflect a binding activity involving 
woven ropes or cords (cf. 1 En. 10:4), which fits the limited context well.  Jastrow (p. 1524) provides the 
related meaning “yarn”. 
13.15: תהמת MQS/GMT/F/AW ]  B3 has apparently skipped this word by mistake.  It is clear on BZ13TM. 
13.16: ̇ ן ̇ מ ֯ ח֯ ו ֯ר ֯ ת֯ר̇ב ̇ ע ]  F ] התא [ ; B3 ֯ ת֯רבע.  B3’s reading seems correct based upon IMneg. x 86-4449, but he and 
others ignore a number of other letters following this word.  The final word appears to be ̇ ן ̇ מ, making it 
likely (but not certain) that the intervening word is חור and arguing against previous reconstructions of 
the beginning of the following line.

13.17: ◌ ◌◌◌ ֯ ם ברעמ ]  MQS/AW ◌ ◌◌ ◌◌ ברעמ ; GMT אחור ברעמ ; F ] אחור ןמ [ ברעמ ; B3 א ֯ חו ֯ר ןמ ברעמ .  The 
proposals of GMT, F and B3 are incorrect, since the letter preceding ברעמ is neither aleph nor final nun.  
A final mem is more likely, but not assured.  This line may begin with the word יד. 
13.18: נא ןמו ̇ ה֯ב ̇ א ◌◌ ] ]  MQS/F/AW ̇ נא ןמו ◌◌ א ;  יחו ֯ר ֯ ע֯ברא ןמו ] א .  The nun of ̇ ה֯בנא is fully preserved in

Column 14:  This column has no top, bottom, or right margins but is attached to col. 15 by its partially intact 
left margin.  Even the available IMneg. photographs appear to have been taken some time after the 
unrolling of the scroll and are in an advanced state of deterioration.  In general, the BZ set is superior 
for this column. 
14.9: ̇ אבר ̇ד ̇י ̇ ה ֯ ו א ]  MQS/AW ̇ב֯ר ◌◌◌ ◌◌◌◌ א ; GMT … ר ב ; F ̇ר ̇ב ] א זראו [ א ; B3 אבר יד את֯ י ֯ ז ֯ ח .  The bottom of the 
word יד, as well as the letter heh, are visible on BZ14T and BZ14M.  There is insufficient room for the 
transcription of B3. 
14.9: ךמלחב B3 ]  MQS/GMT/F/AW םלחב.  The final kaph is plainly seen on BZ14T. 
14.9: ̇םי ֯ר֯ וט MQS/GMT/AW ]  F ̇ וט ̇ר ̇י ̇ א ; B3 ארוט ןד .  Portions of the final mem (especially its right, lower bend 
and left, upper protrusion) are visible on BZ14T. 
14.10: ̇ ח ֯ ת֯ פל א B3 ]  MQS/GMT/F/AW ֯ ח ל ̇ פ א .  If the letter following the lamed is a peh (which is not entirely 
clear), there must be another letter between it and the aleph because of spacing and ink remains.  The left 
portion of an upper, horizontal stroke can be seen near the aleph in BZ14T, suggesting that this is 
probably the emphatic form of אפלח, as in lines 11, 14 and 15.  A tav fits the existing ink remains well. 
14.10: ֯ ן ֯ י ̇ נב ]  MQS/GMT/F/AW ֯ב ] ינ [ ן ; B3 ךינב.  Either reading is possible, since the top of the final letter is

14.10: ̇ מ אי ֯ ן ֯ מ ]  MQS/GMT/F/AW יכ א ◌ ך ; M (margin) ̇ תאוכ ך .  The word אימ is relatively clear on BZ14T. 
14.10: ̇ ג ֯ ל֯ י ̇ צ ]  Four letters appear in the middle of the margin separating cols. 14 and 15 at this point.  The last 
letter, which may have a space between it and the others, is a gimel.  Might this be a mark from scribal 
preparation of the manuscript? 
14.11: םדגב MQS/GMT/F/AW ]  B3 םרגב.  The right horn of the dalet is easily seen on BZ14T and BZ14M. 
14.12: ] ה [ ֯ א ̇ב ̇ר ֯ א֯ י ֯ מ֯ד ֯ ק ]  MQS/F/AW ◌◌◌◌◌◌◌◌◌◌ ◌ ך ; B3 ] ה א [ ֯ב ר ך ֯ א֯ י ֯ מ֯ד ֯ ק .  Despite efforts, I am not able to 
find either of the final kaphs transcribed by MQS/F/AW and B3 in any of the photographs.  There is a 
gaping, horizontal tear in the leather here.  I see possible evidence for only one extended downstroke 
preceding ל̇ ו ̇כ, which I take as the qoph of ֯ א֯ י ֯ מ֯ד ֯ ק.  This word is highly uncertain, but fits the available 
space reasonably well. 
14.12: ̇ ש ̇ך ֯ מ ̇ ן ֯ מ ̇ פ ֯ ה֯ גל ֯כ ] ו [ ל ]  MQS/AW ̇ ש ◌◌ ̇ך ◌ ל ◌◌◌ ל ; GMT ש ] מ [ ך ; F ̇ ש ] מ [ ̇ך ◌ ל ◌◌◌ ל ; B3 ך ֯ מש אל֯ ו לפ֯ י ] .  The 
parchment is split and shrunken here, but it seems that there are actually two final letters very near to 
each other (my final kaph and final nun). 
14.14: ם֯ ו ֯ ק ̇ ק םאי ]  MQS/GMT/F/AW ֯ ם֯ ו ֯ ק ̇ ק ֯ א ם ; B3 םוק֯ י םאק .  The word םאי ̇ ק, along with its medial yod/vav is 
surprisingly clear on BZ14T.  If the preceding םוק is read correctly, this is apparently a rare usage of the 
infinitive absolute plus participle in order to add emphasis. 
14.15: התיזח ̇ פל ̇ ס ֯ ת֯ ג אתפלח ]  MQS/F/AW התיזח ל ◌◌ א אתפלח ; GMT התיזח אתפלחל ; B3 התיזח א ֯ ה֯ד֯ יל אתפלח .  
GMT’s reading is incorrect.  MQS/F/AW read an aleph preceding אתפלח, which is possible (and in 
which case I read אתגספ), but the ink remains actually overlap the following het, and seem more likely to 
be transferred or smeared ink.  The peh and samekh of תגספ are relatively clear, and this word must stand 
in the construct state with אתפלח. 
14.15: ̇ נרחאו ̇י ̇ ת א ]  MQS/F/AW ̇ חאו ̇ר ] תי [ א ; B3 אתירחאו.  The base stroke of the nun is clear in BZ14M.  This is 
a peculiar orthography, and the expected form (אתירחא) may have prejudiced previous readings.  
Perhaps here we see influence from the Hebrew ןורחא? 
14.15: ̇ד ̇י ◌◌◌ ̇ ה֯ נ ֯ מ ]  B3 יד תקפנ הנמ .  There is a hole in the leather (on the BZ photos) where my circlets are 
placed, but there does not appear to be the space or ink remains to support the reading of B3.  IMneg. 
3846 was taken before the hole split apart, but the ink is so blurred that the letters are illegible.

14.16: ◌ ̇ מ ̇ א ̇ ל ֯ פ ֯ א ןמו ]  MQS/F/AW ◌ לא ◌ ןמ ; GMT ןמ.  My suggestion is tentative, but there does appear to be a 
letter between the aleph and lamed transcribed by MQS/F/AW.  The conjunctive vav preceding ןמ is

14.17: ̇ ח ̇ד ̇יל ̇ מ ̇י ̇ ן ̇ר ֯ א אע ̇ חו ד ̇ מ ֯ של ל ֯ א ̇ ע֯ר ֯ א ̇א ]  MQS/GMT/F/AW ◌◌◌◌ ̇ מ ̇ ן ] א [ ר אע ◌◌◌ ל ֯ א ֯ מ ֯ של ◌◌◌ ; B3 [ ןמ ער ֯ א א 
֯ א֯ נ ֯דכ ל ֯ אמ ֯ של ֯ א ֯ ח֯ נ ֯ד ֯ מ .  This entire phrase is discerned with relative ease on BZ14T and BZ14M.  The

14.18: ֯ י ןיבת ]  MQS/F/AW ֯ ה֯ י ןיב .  The lower, left leg and foot of the tav are visible in BZ14T. 
14.19: ̇ ל ̇ ש֯ ה ֯ ל ֯ כת ̇רל ̇ ז א ̇ ה ̇ ו ֯ א֯ ו ]  MQS/F/AW ̇ ח ̇ ו ̇י ת ] ה [ ̇רל ̇ ז א ֯ ד ֯ ע ; M (margin) ̇ ח ̇ ז ̇י ת ] ה [ ̇רל ̇ ז א ֯ד ֯ ע .  This phrase is largely 
effaced on BZ14T and BZ14M, but, when contrast-enhanced, the remains of a lamed can be discerned 
preceding the lamed of א̇ ז ̇רל.  In addition, the two rightmost, slanting arms of a shin are visible preceding 
the tav of ֯ ל ֯ כת ̇ ש֯ ה̇ ל, making התיוח/התיזח improbable.  Just as unlikely is the preposition ֯ד ֯ ע, proposed by 
MQS/F/AW.  I must stress the uncertainty of my own proposal for this word, although the initial heh

lamed of ך ֯ ל is also unsure, and it is possible that these letters should be read as a suffix attached to the 
preceding word. 
14.22: ֯ ל ̇ד ֯ ק ןימ ̇ ש ̇ חל ̇א֯ פ ]  MQS/F/AW ֯ ק ֯ ל ̇ד ןימ ̇ לש ̇ ח ◌◌ .  Two letters attached to the end of ̇ חל ̇ ש are visible in 
BZ14B, making it likely that this word is a form of the shaphel verb ףחלש “to exchange, change.” 
Column 15:  Although parts of each margin are preserved, this column is badly damaged and missing most of 
its upper and lower sections.  Much of the text is eaten away by the corrosive ink in the available photos 
(BZ and IMneg.; IMneg. 3844 and IMneg. x 86-4448 appear to have been taken when the column was 
in slightly better condition). 
15.9: ̇י ̇ ן ֯ י ֯ב֯ב ]  MQS/AW ] [ ̇ ן ; GMT ] ... [ ן ; F ] ה [ ̇ ן ; B3 ן ֯ י ֯ מ֯ ע.  It is clear that there are at least four, and likely five, 
letters in this word.  Two horizontal base strokes, belonging to two bets or similar letters, are visible in 
BZ15T.  In IMneg. 3844 the ink remains of the first letter rule out an ayin (contra B3). 
15.9: ןירוסו ]  MQS/GMT/F/AW ןורוסי; B3 רידקו ןי .  The reading of MQS/GMT/F/AW may, of course, be 
correct, but I have transcribed the word thus because of the preceding word, which is itself uncertain.   
In addition, there is a dot of ink above the penultimate yod/vav, which is likely only an accidental spill.  
B3’s transcription is simply incorrect. 
15.9: ןוהתיגשמ MQS/GMT/F/AW ]  B3 ןוהיניגשמ.  B3 has presumably transcribed this word incorrectly due to 
the ink at the top of the tav (and previous three letters) being eroded away.  In reality, the base stroke of 
the left leg of the tav (B3’s nun) would require the transcription ןוהנייגשמ, and not that of B3. 
15.10: ̇בגל ̇ר ֯ א ̇ב֯ר א ]  MQS/GMT/F/AW/B3 ֯ א֯ר֯בגל.  There is simply too much space for ארבגל alone to be 
written.  This is most evident in IMneg. x 86-4448, where 8-9 letters are clearly discernible (even if some 
of them are difficult to read).  The base stroke of the bet of א̇ב֯ר is also visible in IMneg. x 86-4448. 
15.10: ̇כ ץ̇יצרא ל̇ ו F ]  MQS/AW  ̇ץ̇יצ̇ר ̇ א ◌ ל̇ ו ; B3 ֯ ת֯כ לע אינ֯ זומ֯ ו ] הפ .  A casual glance at BZ15M and BZ15T shows 
that B3’s transcription is impossible (albeit creative), and that there can be no doubt about the proposal 
of MQS et al.  The meaning of this word has troubled commentators (cf. the various translations, or lack 
thereof), but this must begin a descriptive phrase concerning the “great man” mentioned at the 
beginning of the line.  The root ץצר can mean “squeeze, crush,” and is translated by F as “oppress”. 
15.11: אתוב̇ר ה̇ר ̇ מ֯ ו ]  MQS/AW ◌◌◌◌◌ א ̇ ת̇ ו ̇ב ; F ] ר הרמל [ א ̇ ת̇ ו ̇ב ; B3 [ אנ֯ י ֯ד֯ ו .  Although F was correct in his 
reconstruction, he has placed these words at the beginning of the line when there are, in fact, at least 
three words preceding them.  A letter directly preceding the mem of ה̇ר ̇ מ is visible in the photographs, 
but it is too obscured to be read with certainty.  B3’s suggestion is safely ruled out based upon the clear 
base stroke of the bet in אתוב̇ר. 
15.12: ימרו M (margin)/B3 ]  MQS/F ומר̇י; GMT/AW ימרי.  Although any of these options may potentially be 
correct, paleographically ימרו is to be preferred.  The first letter extends even farther down than is 
typical for a vav/yod, while the final letter is particularly short. 
 154 
15.13: ̇ חתיו ̇ב ןו ̇ ת֯ר֯ יק֯דל ]  MQS/GMT/F/AW ֯ ה ֯ תיו ןיב ֯ קל ◌ ; B3 ןוביחתיו אטשוקל .  These words are more difficult 
to read than they first appear.  On IMneg. x 86-4448, the first seven letters appear to form one word.  
The important fourth and fifth letters are likely het and bet, although this is not absolutely certain (I see 
no evidence for an intervening yod, as transcribed by B3).  The second word definitely has one letter 
(dalet or resh) standing between the lamed and qoph, and ends with a tav.  This argues against previous 
transcriptions, yet it remains unclear what this word is or means.  There may be a base stroke (i.e. a bet 
or similar letter) in the penultimate position. 
15.13: ̇רדע ̇ ו ]  MQS/F/AW ע ק֯ י ◌◌ ; B3 א֯ריע.  The reading of MQS/F/AW is understandable when examining 
the manuscript.  The head of the dalet has split apart on several of the photographs, making it look like 
the partial loop of a qoph (but see IMneg. x 86-4448, where the dalet is unmistakeable). The downstroke 
of the following resh, which extends no further down than any of the other letters, was taken instead as 
the qoph’s downstroke.  It is also conceivable that this should be read as the common prepositional 
phrase יד דע. 
15.14: רוש MQS/F/AW ]  B3 דוע.  The shin and resh are abundantly clear on BZ15M. 
15.15: י ֯ מ ֯ מ֯ ע ]  There is a hole in the leather here, distorting all letters but the final yod.  The two middle letters 
(which may even be the first and second of three) have base strokes typical of mem, bet or other such 
characters.  Another possibility is י ֯ב֯ב֯ר. 
15.16: ̇ גגשו ן ֯ ה ]  MQS/F/AW איגשו ן ; B3 [ ֯ ן ֯ י ןיאיגש .  The left leg of the second gimel is partially effaced, but the 
joint is very comparable to that preceding it (and is too low for the stroke interchange of a yod).  The heh 
is also obscured, but discernible.  Each photograph has proven helpful for this word, depending on 
which letters is being examined. 
15.16: ֯ב מ ̇ ף ֯ד֯ ג ]  The superscripted mem is most visible on BZ15M. 
15.18: ןישבתשמו ]  B3 ן ֯ י ֯ שמ ֯ שמ֯ ו.  This word is made out with certainty on BZ15M. 
15.19: לע ̇ ח אמל ̇ד ן B3 ]  MQS/F/AW הילע אמל ◌ ן .  B3 is to be credited with this perceptive reading, which is 
most easily distinguished on IMneg. x 86-4448. 
15.19: ̇י ̇ ה ̇י ̇ הבר ]  MQS/F/AW ◌◌ ֯ הב֯רי ; B3 אה הברי .  The first three letters of this aphel verb are discernible in all 
of the photos, especially when the contrast is enhanced. 
15.20: ךתיוחא B3 ]  MQS/F/AW ךניוחא.  The tav is clear in BZ15M. 
15.22: ̇ ם ֯ של ירב ו ̇ וכ אל M (margin) ]  MQS/F/AW ל ◌◌◌ ידב יכז ◌ אל .  The best photograph here is BZ15B, 
where the reading of the last two words is relatively clear despite the damaged parchment.  The word 
םשל was first suggested by M, and makes good sense in this context. 
Column 16:  Col. 16 is the last of this sheet of parchment, and is significantly narrower than those surrounding 
it.  Like the preceding columns, it is missing a sizable portion of its upper and lower parts.  The BZ 
photos for this column are washed out in places, but but remain very valuable in others.  In general, the 
IMneg. set is read more easily. 
16.9: ֯ד ̇ מ̇י א ]  MQS/GMT/F/AW נ ֯ של ̇ א ; B3 כ [ א֯ י ֯ פ ; Esh [ א֯ ינ ֯ של .  Whatever the letter preceding the aleph, it is not 
a nun or yod. On BZ16M and IMneg. 3844 there is a clear upper, horizontal stroke, assuring that it is 
either a kaph or a mem.  Graphically, the letter looks more like a typical kaph, but the following mem of ןמ 
looks very similar, and a mem makes better sense of the word.  It is preceded by the bottom of a short, 
vertical stroke – almost surely a yod.  I see no clear evidence of a lamed at the beginning of the word in 
any of the photographs. 
16.9: ןוהיניב MQS/GMT/F/B3/AW ] Esh ןהיניב.  The penultimate vav is plainly visible on BZ16T, BZ16M, 
and IMneg. x 86-4450. 
16.9: ̇ מ ̇ק ֯ ח ]  MQS/F/AW/Esh ̇ עב ̇י ̇ ן ; GMT ןיעמ; B3 ןועמ.  Scrutiny of the photographs certifies that previous 
readings are not correct.  First, the initial letter is definitely not a bet (contra MQS/F/AW), but quite 
possibly a mem.  In IMneg. x 86-4450 and BZ16M the upper part of this letter, with its characteristic 
upward slanting (from left to right) stroke and small horn in the upper, righthand corner, is plainly seen.  
This judgment is confirmed when closely compared with mems from this and surrounding lines.  It 
appears that the slanting, upper stroke of this mem has been mistaken as the rightmost stroke of an ayin 
 155 
by others.  Second, the last letter is not a final nun, as transcribed in previous editions, but a qoph.  This is 
especially clear on IMneg. 3884, but can be discerned on any of the photographs by examining the 
letter’s lower extension in comparison with surrounding qophs and final nuns (the qoph of קבד, almost 
directly under this word, provides the nearest parallel).  The nun has a characteristic right to left curve at 
the end of the tail, while the qoph is straight throughout. When these factors are taken into account, it is 
most plausible that the central letter is a heh or het, the right leg of which has been taken by previous 
readers as the left stroke of the ayin.  The left leg has been transcribed as a yod/vav.  This is further 
confirmed by a horizontal stroke connecting the two legs at the top, visible in IMneg. 3845.  Perhaps the 
most convincing refutation of the proposals ןיעב and ןיעמ is a simple comparison with the assured 
occurrence of ב / ןיעכ later in the line. 
This leads to my proposed ̇ ק ֯ ח ̇ מ, which appears to be a parallel to the “Mauk Sea” of Jub. 8:22, 26, 
exhibiting a spelling similar to a Syriac Chronicle containing this portion of Jubilees ( ; cf. 
VanderKam, The Book of Jubilees, I.266 and II.54 [n. to 8:22], who argues for the Syriac being a better 
witness to the text at this point).  In fact, when it is recognized that the Genesis Apocryphon is 
describing Japheth’s allotment in the opposite direction as Jub. 8:25-29, it becomes clear that this 
reference fits nicely with the placement of the Mauk in Jubilees. 
16.9: ̇ר̇בעו ]  B3 דועו.  The base stroke of the bet is seen clearly in IMneg. x 86-4450. 
16.9: כ ןיע M (margin) ]  MQS/GMT/F/AW/B3/Esh ב ןיע .  The letters bet and kaph look very similar in this 
portion of the manuscript, and while the first letter of this word has an angular bend at its lower, right 
corner (presumably causing others to transcribe it as bet), there are nearby instances (e.g. אהלוכ in line 
10) where an assured kaph has the very same characteristic.  In fact, if any single factor distinguishes bet 
from kaph in this section of the scroll it is the height of each letter – the bet being shorter and more 
compressed than the kaph.  If this is taken into account, the present letter should certainly be read as a 
kaph.  Furthermore, when compared to the word in line 17, transcribed by all as ןיעכ, one recognizes 
that almost no difference exists between the first letters of each the two.  Whatever one judges this letter 
to be, the two words should be read the same.  In addition to this paleographic reasoning, I prefer kaph 
because a geographic adverb seems plausible in both cases, and a translation such as “regarding sight” 
(cf. the use of ןי ֶ ְכ in Ezek 1, 8:2, 10:9 and Dan 10:6) or “as a spring” (so F) makes the best sense in this 
context.  Interestingly, M appears to have corrected his initial reading of ןיעב to ןיעכ in the margin of the 
copy of his M.A. thesis available in the Judaica Reading Room of the University and National Library at 
the Hebrew University of Jerusalem, Givat Ram. 
16.9: א̇ נ ̇כ֯ר֯ וא ]  Another word plainly follows ןיעכ at the end of the line in BZ16M, and especially BZ16T. 
16.11: ֯ גל ] ד [ ̇ר א ]  MQS/AW ̇ אל ◌◌ א ; GMT/F ̇ גל ] ד י [ ̇ר א ; B3 אל ] ר [ א֯ ע ; Esh א֯ריד֯ גל.  The gimel and resh are badly 
damaged, but fit the remaining ink traces well.  I do not find enough space for both dalet and yod, as 
reconstructed by GMT/F/Esh.  The penultimate letter is definitely not an ayin, as transcribed by B3.  
Esh has apparently forgotten to add brackets around the letters dalet and yod. 
16.12: ̇ נ֯ ו ̇ ו ̇ ח ̇קל ֯ ח ]  MQS/GMT/F/AW ̇קל ֯ ח; B3 ] יד [ קלח .  There is a wide, horizontal crack running through 
these words, and the bottom portion has shrunk and shifted significantly in relation to the top.  MQS et 
al. begin the line with קלח, but when looking below the crack it becomes obvious that other letters 
precede this word.  Once this is recognized, the letters nun, vav and het/heh may be made out, supplying 
the subject of the verb.  This reading was arrived at with the gracious assistance of E. Eshel. 
16.12: ̇י ̇ר ̇ תו ת MQS/GMT/F/AW ]  B3 ת֯ ותרי.  The order of the last three letters, and especially the vav, is 
evident in all of the photographs. 
16.12: ̇ם֯ י ̇ מ̇ ל ֯ ע ]  Slight traces of a lamed may precede this word. 
16.15: ̇ב ֯ד ֯ ע ] ]  B3 ד דע ] י .  The letter following the (uncertain) word דע has a base stroke, and should be read as 
a bet despite the frequent employment of the prepositional phrase יד דע throughout this section. 
16.17: ̇י ם B3 ]  MQS/GMT/F/AW ] ל [ םי .  There is a vertical split in the leather along the margin line, but I do 
not see evidence of a lamed preceding the word םי. 
 156 
16.17: ןיעכ MQS/GMT/F/AW/B3 ]  Esh ןיעב.  See note to 16.9 above.  Eshel (41, n. 16) mentions ןיעכ as F’s 
reading alone, but it is also espoused by MQS and others.  The initial letter, which she reads as bet, is 
indeed “clearly visible”.. That it is a bet is less sure, however.  Like the same word in line 9, the letter is 
taller than a typical bet in this part of the scroll, and almost certainly is a kaph. 
16.17: ימ ̇ של ̇ נ ֯ א ]  MQS/F/AW ̇ ןמ ̇ של ֯ א֯ נ ; GMT ןמ ... ; B3 ימ הנעל .  B3 is correct in transcribing ימ, as seen on 
any of the photographs (but see especially BZ16M).  The join between the two leftmost strokes of the 
shin is visible on IMneg. 3845, especially when the contrast is enhanced. 
16.18: ל אמי ן ֯ ש ]  F ] זאו [ ת ל ] ח [ ̇ ו ̇ מ ̇ א .  F’s reconstruction is untenable, since the final nun preceding אמי is plainly 
seen on BZ16M. 
16.18: ̇ צמל ֯ר ] י [ ֯ ן ]  MQS/GMT/F/AW ̇ מל ̇ ע ֯ב֯ר ; B3 א ֯ ח֯ נ ֯דמל.  This word is badly eroded, with only the very tops 
(and a few other bits) of the letters remaining.  The best photo is IMneg. x 86-4450, where the top of 
the tsade is very clear, and too high relative to the surrounding letters to be the valley of an ayin.  A 
“Branch of the Egyptian Sea” is mentioned in the parallel account of Jub 8:14. 
Column 17:  This column begins a new sheet of parchment containing 34-35 lines per column.  It is in similar 
condition as col. 16, although less of the top and bottom margins remain.  It is also among the wider 
columns of the scroll.  A qoph, written in a scribal hand very different than that of the scroll’s main text, 
is easily seen in the upper, righthand corner of this sheet.  The BZ photos are again more washed out 
than the IMneg. set but prove useful in several crucial areas. 
17.7: ֯ ג ֯ ל ֯ פ GMT/F ]  MQS/B3/AW ֯ י ֯ר֯ב.  There is almost nothing left of these letters, save some slight ink 
remains of their lower parts.  The first letter could be either bet or peh, while the others are too 
fragmentary to reach a definite conclusion.  Supplying a verb, along with GMT/F, seems to me the 
better option (cf. Jub 9:2a and F, 173). 
17.7: א ֯ מיל GMT/F ]  MQS/AW יל ◌ ] י [ ̇ מ א ; B3 יל ] אמ ד [ א֯ נ .  There is a vertical crack along the margin, and it 
appears that the word אמיל has simply pulled apart at the mem. 
17.8: ו ̇ב ֯ ת ] הר [ ]  MQS/GMT/F/AW ̇ סו ר ֯ ח ; B3 ֯ גסו ] ה [ .  The second letter of this word does not resemble a 
samekh.  The lower, right corner (which should be gently sloping from right to left if MQS et al. are 
correct) is clearly the angular corner of a bet, mem, kaph or nun.  Nor does the spacing favor reading 
הגסו/רחסו, which would fall short of filling the available space.  Both the spacing and ink remains 
support reconstructing הרתבו, as at the end of the line. 
17.8: אלקדחל ... ̇ר ֯ ת֯ב֯ ו ֯ ה ]  AY (22/טי) לקדחל ... ; MQS/F/AW לקדחל ◌◌◌◌◌◌◌◌◌◌ ֯ ה֯ר ֯ ת֯ב֯ו ; B3 לקדחל ֯ ה֯ נ ] אר 
תבו [ ֯ ה֯ר ] לח [ ק ֯ ה ֯ מע ] ו [ ֯ ן .  The remaining ink traces and spacing do not correspond to B3’s suggested 
reading.  The articular aleph at the end of לקדחל is plain on BZ17T and IMneg. x 86-4450, making it less 
likely that ארהנ followed this word.  הרתבו fits well the existing tops of the letters at the end of the line.  
This possibility is further strengthened by the following םראל, which would mirror the repetitive syntax 
of this section. 
17.9: ̇ ה ֯ר֯ ו ] טר [ ]  MQS/F/AW ] רושא [ .  It is quite clear on BZ17T that the word following רוט is not רושא.  
Rather, the word begins with two parallel vertical strokes (of which only the bottoms are visible), which 
I read as a heh.  This is followed by another vertical stroke, which appears to be a resh or dalet, making the 
designation טררוה likely.  Ararat is mentioned as a range elsewhere in the scroll (cf. 10.12; 12.8), but as a 
single mountain here and in 17.14. 
17.9: תירקב ̇ד ֯ א ̇ ו ̇ב ̇ר ֯ ת ̇ ה ̇ד֯ ולל ◌ ̇ ט ]  MQS/F/AW ̇ב ק ◌ ̇ ה ◌◌◌◌◌◌◌◌◌ ̇רא ̇ר ̇ ה ̇ ל ◌◌ ט ; B3 ה֯רק֯ב ] ◌◌◌ [ הרתבו טקיל ] ן [ .  
The first two words close the description of Aram’s portion, the word תירקב being especially clear on 
BZ17T.  The end of this line solves the problem of where Lud fits into the apportionment among 
Shem’s sons.  In IMneg. x 86-4450 the final three words are read with much more confidence than in 
BZ17T, where the letters are badly skewed and blurred.  There is no sign of a qoph (or final nun), as 
transcribed by B3, which is one of several reasons that his reading should be rejected.  The letters 
following ̇ד̇ ולל, at the end of the line, are enigmatic and difficult to contextualize.  The tet is quite certain, 
and I had first read ̇ט֯ ל, although it is unclear what this might mean.  I continue to wonder if the scribe 
 157 
had begun a word (e.g. רוטל – note the phrase at the beginning of the next line), but then abandoned it 
for some reason. 
17.10: ןד אברעמל B3 ]  MQS/F/GMT/AW ̇ ו ̇ א ל֯ ז אברעמ .  These words are easily recognizable on BZ17T. 
17.10: ֯כ ו ל ל ] די [ ̇ א֯ נ ֯ של ]  MQS/F/AW לו ◌◌ ; B3 ֯ תלו ] ו [ ל ֯ב .  There seems to be too much space and ink for גוגמ 
alone to precede the yod/vav of my לו ֯כ.  The lamed of לו ֯כ is followed directly by another in BZ17T, 
although its upper portion is effaced.  Mention of Tubal (B3) makes very little sense at this point in the 
description, while the next line seems to require previous mention of a ןשל – hence, my ̇ א֯ נ ֯ של.  In 
general, the last half of this line is in very poor shape. 
17.10: ... ̇ ו ל ̇ד ֯ י ̇י ֯ב ם ]  MQS/F/AW ... לו ◌◌◌ םי ; B3 ם֯ ו ֯רדלו.  While B3’s reading is not impossible (albeit the spacing 
does not seem quite right to me), it seems better to take this as a mention of an “Eastern Sea.”  This 
would make better sense in connection with א̇ נ̇ ו ̇ פ֯ צ ֯ב at the beginning of the next line (what would the 
phrase “and to the southeast in the north” signify?).  If correct, this must be a reference to the modern 
Caspian Sea. 
17.11: לעד MQS et al. ]  AY (22/טי) לעו.  Although irregular in the scroll’s morphology, there is no doubt that 
here the relative pronoun יד has elided with the preposition לע (cf. also 17.7; 20.7; 21.29; 22.14, 21). 
17.11: ̇דל ̇ מור ] א [ ̇ד ן ]  MQS/GMT/F/AW ̇יל ̇ד ̇י ̇ מ ֯ א ן ֯ד ; B3 מורדל ] ה [ ןו .  B3 is certainly correct in reading the 
second letter as a dalet rather than a yod, since the head of the letter (with its two horns) is easily seen on 
IMneg. x 86-4450.  Hence, we must have here a directional reference to “south.”  This makes good 
sense in describing Lud’s portion, which we would expect to run along the north of the “three portions” 
(i.e. Aram, Asshur, and Arpachshad) mentioned in this line.  MQS et al. appear to be correct, however, 
in reading the penultimate letter as a dalet (or resh – the upper, righthand corner is missing) rather than 
yod/vav.  This is best seen on IMneg. x 86-4450 and BZ17T. 
17.12: ל ◌◌◌◌◌◌ ]  MQS/F/AW ל ] מוחת [ ֯א ; B3 ל ] אמוחת [ .  The suggestion of MQS et al. does not fit the ink 
traces or the context particularly well.  The spacing, however, is approximately correct for their 
reconstruction. 
17.13: אנשל וגב יד איאו MQS/GMT/F/AW ]  B3 ימו רענש לוכב יד א .  This entire phrase is abundantly clear on 
IMneg. x 86-4450 and BZ17M, despite B3’s lack of diacritical marks. 
17.14: ̇ מ ֯ אל ̇ נ א ֯ צ ֯ד ̇ מ ̇ד֯ י ]  MQS/F/AW/B3 ̇ נ ֯בל ֯ י ̇ ג ̇מ֯ ו ̇ר .  I find the proposal of MQS et al. completely unconvincing.  
Following the lamed, a mem (possibly bet) can be made out, yet it is at least one letter space removed from 
the lamed (hence, my aleph).  In addition, my mem is quite clearly followed by the letters nun and aleph.  
The following word is less certain, but the relatively sure טררה two words later makes a relational 
preposition or verb such as this plausible.  דימצד fits the remaining ink traces fairly well, although a 
possible vertical stroke before the mem continues to give me pause. 
17.16: הרתבו MQS et al. ]  AY (22/טי) הרתכו.  The word is הרתב, as elsewhere. 
17.17: ̇ד ̇ב רבע ]  MQS/AW ◌◌ ̇ר̇ב ̇ ע ; F/B3 ] ד י [ ̇ ע ̇ב ̇ר .  The initial letters dalet and bet/mem are discernible in 
BZ17M, ruling out the proposal of F/B3.  Although the second letter may possibly be a mem, this does 
not greatly alter the meaning.  The base word is apparently the noun רבע “border, side,” preceded by a 
compound preposition, used in a manner similar to the biblical expression רבעמ/ב “on the other side, 
beyond, across from.”  If correct, this phrase is paralleled in Jub. 9:11, where Tubal receives “the other 
side of the second branch.”  A defective aphel participle is less plausible, as is a pael form, which typically 
carries more idiomatic meanings (e.g. “be with child”). 
17.18: ל ] אנש [ ךשמל ̇ א֯ נ ֯ א֯ י ֯ נ ֯ ת ]  MQS/F/AW [ ךשמל֯ ו ̇ א̇ ע̇ר ̇ א̇ב ; B3 ל ] אוג [ ךשמל אער ֯ א֯ד .  Very little remains of the 
first two words, and it must be admitted that any of the proposed readings is possible.  My suggestion 
does not contradict the physical remains, and is based partially on Jub. 9:11.  There is definitely no vav 
preceding the lamed of ךשמל. 
17.18:  ̇ א֯ ע̇ב֯ר ֯ א ] ואגנ [ ֯ ת ]  My restoration follows Jub. 9:13. 
17.18:  ̇ד̇יל הל ]  MQS/F/AW ̇ ל ◌ ̇ ן ̇ ש̇ ל ;  ב ] וכ [ ןשל ל .  The heh of הל is clear in BZ17M, and I see no evidence for a 
final letter.  In addition, it is obvious in all the photographs that there are one to two letters standing 
between the two lameds. 
 158 
17.19: ] וח דיל קבד יד אמי [ ק ֯ ל ]  MQS/AW ] יד אמי ח דיל [ ̇ק ֯ ל ; F ] וח דיל יד אמי [ ̇ ל ̇ק ; B3 וח [ קל .  The reconstruction 
offered by MQS/AW and F would not adequately fill the damaged area of the manuscript, which is why 
I also reconstruct the word קבד.  F/B3’s proposed קלוח (versus MQS/AW’s קלח) better conforms to 
the morphology of this word in the scroll. 
17.19: לע [ ֯ א֯ י ֯ מ ]  MQS/F/AW [ ◌◌ ֯א֯ ל .  This area is badly damaged, and the ink smeared.  My reading accords 
with the parallel section ending at 16.12. 
Column 18:  While a large portion of the middle of this column is extant, the leather itself has been almost 
completely destroyed by the ink, leaving nothing but the long shreds of leather intact between each line.  
Because of this, there is nothing left to recover but stray letters here and there.  The right and bottom 
margins are completely missing. 
Column 19:  This column resumes once again the columns first published by AY, and has, therefore, been 
commented upon by many more scholars than most of the preceding columns.  It has been 
conventional to follow the line numbering of AY for this column, even though it has been observed 
multiple times their numbering is one line off (e.g. line 7 should actually be line 6).  I have chosen to 
adhere to this convention in order to avoid confusion.  The plate of this column in AY (i.e. IMneg. 
3856) remains very useful, but recourse to the scaleable photos of the IMneg. and BZ sets has proven 
crucial in certain cases.  For the remaining columns the BZ photographs show the scroll with a netting 
over it, presumably intended to help keep the leather in-tact. 
19.7: ◌ ̇ ק ]   [ ֯ א ֯ ל ◌◌◌ ̇ ן ֯ י ]  J/F/AW ]  חבדמ ןמת תינבו [ א .  A final nun is easily identified preceding the word ת̇ירק̇ ו 
in IMneg. 3856 and BZ19TM.  This rules out the reconstruction first suggested by J and followed by 
F/AW.  AW has apparently made a curious scribal error by placing this reconstruction in line 6 instead 
of line 7, as it is situated (but not numbered) in J.  This may be due to the confusion mentioned in the 
previous note. 
19.8: ל ֯ א ... דב ֯ אמל ]  J/GMT/AW ] א [ ל ] יה א [ ל ] ה ע [ ל ] אימ ןמתו ה [ לל ] ת תכרבו , הרמ וכ [ ל םימלע ; B1 ] .. [ םל ֯ חמל יד ; 
Du-So/Mi-To/F ל ] י א [ ל ] ע [ ל ] אמ הו [ לל ] ת [ הל ̇ על ̇ימל ̇ם ] רב [ ̇ם ; B3 ] ע [ ל ] אי א [ ל ] ה [ ימלע ] א ◌◌ מו [ ֯ התלל ] ימע 
התרמאו ◌ [ םל ֯ חמל .  It is difficult to know where to begin when critiquing previous reconstructions of 
this line, but it must be admitted at the outset that the beginning several words are almost entirely 
missing and may never be recovered with any certainty.  Consideration of all the photographic evidence 
proves every reconstruction to date untenable, and unfortunately reveals more about what is not there 
than what is.  Rather than try to reconstruct a coherent text in this line (my actual readings should be 
viewed as tentative) I have attempted to reflect as accurately as possible the extant letter remains and 
spacing.  This is no small task, since many parts of the line have split and pulled away from each other.  
Particularly troubling is the reconstruction of Du-So/Mi-To/F, who seem to have spent very little time 
assessing the spacing of the line.  For instance, I can find no grounds for their transcription ̇ם̇ימל ̇ על הל 
at this point in the line.  Furthermore, it can be clearly seen in BZ19TM and IMneg. 3856 that the letter 
preceding דע is not a final mem, but a dalet.  The proposal of J/GMT/AW is slightly better, but still far 
from accurate, while that of B1/3 is impossible.  Suffice to say that at any point in this line where I differ 
in transcription with any of the previous reconstructions (which is nearly every letter) it is purposeful 
and meant as a rejection of their reading.  The word דב ֯ אמל seems an allusion to the mantra that the 
Israelites are commanded to recite in Deut. 26:5, “A wandering Aramean (דבא ימרא) was my father…,” 
which also refers to the descent of Abram into Egypt. 
19.9: ל ] המ [ ֯ך ◌◌ ]  AY/B1/F/AW ל ]       [ ; J ל ] הירומ [ .  J’s reconstruction appears unlikely.  The lower 
extension of what is probably a final letter is visible in the fourth position on BZ19TM, and there also 
seems to be too much space for the word הירומל alone.  The same phrase is used in 19.10-11. 
19.9: ̇ מ ̇אמורדל ֯ ו ̇ר ֯ ה ◌ ◌◌ תיתא֯ ו ֯ א דע  ]  AY ̇ אמורדל ]     [ א ]       [ דע ; J  אמורדל ]       [ א ◌◌ דע ; F  ̇ אמורדל ] ו [ ̇ תא ] תי [ 
דע; B1/GMT/AW  אמורדל ] ... [ דע ֯ ת֯ יתא֯ ו .  On all of the photos it is clear that there are at least two 
intervening words between those transcribed successively by F.  The first word is not certain, but agrees 
with Gen 12:6, where Abram camps at the Oak of Moreh and receives a visitation from the Lord.  This 
has implications for the debate (cf. F, p. 180) whether אשידק ארוט, at the end of the previous line, refers 
 159 
the mountain east of Bethel (Gen 12:8), or Jerusalem, arguing strongly for the former.  It should be 
noted that Jub. 13:5-7, 15 also makes much of the same mountain, between Bethel and Ai. 
19.9: ֯ ו ב ̇ ן ̇ד ̇ הנ̇י ֯ד ֯ מל ] נ [ תאי ]  AY/J ◌ ל ]       [ ב ̇ ת̇ א ] נ [ תאי ; GMT/F/AW ל̇ ו ] ז ה [ ב ̇ ת̇ א ̇ א̇ נ ̇ מ ] נ [ תאי ; B1  ֯ד֯ ו ֯ ע ֯ אל֯ ו
 בתא ] נ [ תאי .  IMneg. 3856 and BZ19TM reveal beyond doubt that previous proposals are not correct.  
IMneg. 3856 shows a broad base stroke (my mem) following the lamed, while it is also clear that the letter 
preceding the nun is not a mem (cf. F’s ז [ ̇ א̇ נ ̇ מ ).  A final letter is visible preceding the bet of ב ] נ [ תאי , which 
renders the transcription ב ̇ ת̇ א ] נ [ תאי impossible.  Hence, it seems that here we have reference to Abram 
himself founding the city of Hebron, which may also be the implication of Jub 13:10 “When he reached 
Hebron (Hebron was built at that time), he stayed there for two years.” 
19.10: ̇ אל̇ וכ AY/J/GMT/F/AW ]  B1 וכ ל ֯ ה ֯ א .  There is not enough space for a heh between the lamed and aleph. 
19.10: ̇ ע ] וב [ ̇ ו ֯ ה א̇ר ] א [ J/GMT/AW ]  AY ֯ ט ] ב [ א ֯ ת֯ ו ]     [ ; B1 ֯ ג ֯ ש א֯ ע֯ב ֯ ש ] י [ ; Gin/Mu1/F ̇ ע ] וב [ א ̇ר ] יתי [ .  Ginsberg 
was the first to suggest that the initial letter has the shape of an ayin rather than tet (cf. AY), and this 
judgment appears correct (see especially IMneg. 3856).  J/GMT/AW were correct in placing an aleph at 
the end of the word, since in both BZ19TM and IMneg. 3856 the resh and aleph can be seen touching 
each other. 
19.11:  ֯ך ֯ המ̇ ל ◌ ]  [ ןירצמ̇ב֯ד ̇ ה̇ ע̇ר ̇ אל ]  J/GMT/AW ל ] לעמ [ עראל ןירצמ ; B1 ל ] ךהמ [ ֯ ע֯ר ֯ א ֯ ו ֯ גל ןירצמ ; F ל מ ] ךה [ עראל 
מ ןירצ .  There is more text to be accounted for at the beginning of this line than any of the earlier 
transcriptions reflect.  The first word is far from certain, but matches the remaining traces of ink, while 
there is certainly a bet preceding ןירצמ, and probably yet another letter. 
19.11: אנומר̇כל AY/J/GMT/F/AW ]  B1 אנומרנל.  The top of the second letter is partially effaced, but does 
not appear to be a nun (cf. IMneg. 3856). 
19.12: ןעכ AY/J/B1/GMT/F ]  AW ןפכ.  AW’s transcription is incorrect. 
19.13: כל ̇ ה אנ ]  AY/J/B1/GMT/F/AW אנפל ̇ ח.  It is surprising that the kaph, which is entirely visible in 
BZ19TM, has been overlooked by so many commentators.  It is, however, more difficult to discern on 
the original plates of AY than on other photographs.  G. Anderson and P. Beaulieu have helpfully 
pointed out that the root ךלה is used in the sense of “go out” in Gen 26:26, as well as in Assyrian texts. 
19.14: ֯ ילעמ J/B1/GMT/F/AW ]  AY ֯ א֯ נלעמ.  The spacing appears to fit ילעמ best,  although the end of the 
word is badly damaged. 
19.15: ֯ ח ֯ מ̇ צ ̇ א̇ד ֯ ח̇כ אדח ] ו [ ֯ ש ̇ ן ̇ מ ̇ר ] דח ש [ B1 ]  AY/J אדח ]     [ א ]           [ ; F  אדח ] יאי [ ̇ ג ̇ש ̇ א ] י [ ; AW מצ אדחכ ] וח [ 
֯ר ֯ ש ןמ ] דח ש [ .  B1’s reading is plausible, although it remains far from certain.  F’s reading fits neither the 
available space nor the ink remains, and AW has forgotten the word אדח. 
19.15: ̇ ק̇ב ̇ ש̇ מל̇ ו B1/Qim1/GMT/F/AW ]  AY/Kut/J ̇ק̇ ו ̇ב ̇ ש̇ מל̇ ו.  The letters bet and qoph are directly next to each 
other, leaving no room for a vav.  See Qim1 (pp. 14-15) or Ck (p. 372) for further discussion. 
19.16:  ןמ אנירת ̇שרש Gin2/J/B1/GMT/F/AW ]  AW ̇אדש ןמ אפירת.  This reading is recognizable even on the 
original plates of AY, although more certainty is gained by consulting BZ19TM.  The words following 
these have been the subject of much speculation in the past (cf. F, p. 186), but are now quite widely 
agreed upon.  The spacing is acceptable for these and the following words, despite Mu2’s objection (p. 
44). 
19.17:  ̇ אלו ֯ י ֯ נ֯ ו ̇ צ ̇ צ ̇ ק ]  AY  אלו ]   [ ; J/GMT/AW  אלו ] ץקתא [ ; B1  אלו ] ץיצא [ ; Qim1 ̇ץ ̇ ק ̇ תאלו; F ̇ץ ̇ק ̇ ת<א> אלו.  These 
words are very faint on the manuscript, but the first six letters can be recovered with relative certainty by 
enhancing the brightness and contrast of BZ19BM.  The aleph and qoph are read as one word (with an 
intervening tav) by Qim1/F, although F must emend the reading to ̇ץ ̇ ק ̇ ת<א> אלו in order to make sense 
of it.  Such close proximity of words is not uncommon in the scroll, and, despite F’s claim to the 
contrary, there is no evidence of a tav between what is quite clearly an aleph and a qoph.  The final word is 
longer than even Qimron recognized, although the final two or three letters are unclear even with 
modification.  The penultimate letter appears to have a single, upright stroke, making it probable that 
here we have an object suffix referring to either the cedar tree alone (ינ-) or both the cedar and date 
palm (אנ-) attached to a peal 3 pl. perf. verb from ץצק. 
 160 
19.18: מ ֯ ן ] ד [ ̇ נא לחד ֯ ה ]  AY  ֯ ןמ ◌◌ א ] או [ לחד ; J/GMT/AW ] או הנא [ לחד ; Mu1/F ̇ ו א ] הנ [ לחד ; B1 ע֯כ ֯ ןמ ] ן [ לחד ֯ א .  
The suggestions of J/GMT/AW and Mu1/F may be ruled out by the certainty of the mem after ̇ ת̇ מל ̇ ח, 
which is apparent on BZ19BM.  Following ֯ ןמ (the nun of which is almost completely effaced) there is 
room for an intervening letter before the aleph of ֯ ה̇ נא. I propose a dalet here, which would make sense of 
the phrase and agree with syntactic convention in the scroll (cf. 0.11; 22.29).  There is no physical 
evidence of an aphel form of the verb לחד (contra B1), while a participle is quite coherent in this context.  
The spacing for several of the proposed readings, in particular J/GMT/AW and Mu1/F, is not even 
close to accurate.  Given the above factors, it is remarkable that the reconstruction of J has been carried 
over into the recent texts of GMT and AW. 
19.18: אמלח al. ]  AY המלח.  The aleph is clear in all of the photographs and has been duly noted by a number 
of commentators (cf. F, p. 187). 
19.19: ֯ ת̇רמ ̇ א֯ ו ל ] ה [ ̇ מ ]      [ ֯ ן ]  J/GMT/AW ] תיוחו [ ל ] רשפ ה [ ; B1  ֯ ת֯ר ֯ מ ֯ א֯ ו ◌◌◌◌◌◌◌ ; F ] התיוחו [ ל ] רשפו ה [ .  The 
reconstructions of J/GMT/AW and F do not adequately fit the ink traces visible on BZ19TM and 
BZ19BM, in which the aleph and mem of ֯ ת̇רמ ̇ א֯ ו are clearly visible (as is the mem following ל ] ה [ , when 
contrast is enhanced).  Furthermore, the lower extension of a final letter preceding אמלח renders the 
reconstruction רשפ untenable. All three of the previous proposals are also a bit short in relation to the 
available space. 
19.19: ̇ א ◌◌◌ ◌◌ ֯ ט֯ר ◌◌◌ ֯ ן ]  AY/J/B1 א ]      [ ; GMT/AW ] ו [ מא ] תר [ ◌◌◌ ; F מא ] ר [ ת ◌◌◌ .  There are more letters 
here than is reflected in previous readings, and I do not see convincing evidence for the word תרמא.  
The vav of GMT/AW is definitely not present. 
19.19: םר֯ב Gin/J/Pu/Qim1/GMT/F/AW/B3 ]  AY ] יב [ םו ; B1 ם ֯ ח֯ב.  Gin, J, GMT and AW reconstruct the bet, 
which is no longer necessary.  Although a hole has disintegrated most of the bet, all three letters can be 
discerned on BZ19BM (the last two clearly). 
19.20: ̇ ת֯ ו ֯ר ̇ ע ]  AY ]      [ ; Gin/J/F ] רתא [ ; B1/GMT/AW ֯ר ֯ ת֯ א.  The word רתא is not correct.  A hole has 
destroyed part of each of the letters, but in BZ19TM the last letter clearly has a left leg, which appears to 
belong to a tav.  In any case, it is not a resh.  The first letter has the right to left, sloped stroke of an ayin, 
while the two (or perhaps one?) middle letters, of which only the very tops remain, are compatible with 
my reading. 
19.20: ] התנ [ ֯ ל ] ןה [ ]  Gin ] ןמתל התנ [ ; J/F ] הב הוהנ [ ; B1/GMT/AW ] ל ךהנ [ ֯ ה .  My own reconstruction is 
obviously very tenuous but draws attention to some shortcomings of earlier suggestions.  For example, 
the upper remains of a lamed are visible (ruling out the proposal of J/F), and there appear to be two 
letters between it and the aleph of ירמא.  Fortunately, the basic meaning is clear from the surrounding 
context. 
19.20: ֯ ה ̇ חאו B1/F ]  AY/Gin/J/GMT/AW ̇י ̇ חאו.  The ink traces seem to cover too large an area to be those of 
a yod, although there is a hole in the leather here. 
19.20: יכילטב AY/Gin/J/GMT/F/AW ]  B1 יכילידב.  The tet is obvious in all photographs. 
19.22: ̇ ו ֯ ע̇ צ וער ̇ פ ] ן J/B1/GMT/F/AW ]  AY יעדפ ̇ א.  The letters following this phrase, combined with the clarity 
of the reading on BZ19BM, leave no doubt that this is a reference to Pharaoh Zoan. 
19.22: ◌◌ ̇י ̇ ע ירש ]  AY/F [ יר ̇ ש̇ ו ; J/GMT/AW ◌◌◌ ירש ; B1 ירש יג ֯ ש.  What I have read as yod at the end of the 
word preceding ירש may equally be placed at the beginning of the next word (where it would be read as 
a vav), as AY/F propose.  B1’s יג ֯ ש is not correct, since on BZ19BM it is clear that his gimel does not have 
the righthand leg required by that letter.  In addition, the letter preceding it does not have the 
characteristics of a sin.  This may instead be a verb meaning something like “be reluctant, fear,” referring 
to Sarai’s reticence to go to Zoan.  F’s reconstructed דוע אל, earlier in the line, does not appear correct 
due to the lower extension of a final letter following the lamed. 
19.23: ◌◌◌ ] ו        [ ֯ ת֯ ל ֯ ח֯ד ]  J/GMT/AW ] תרמתסהו ימע [ ; F ] תלחד ירא ימע [ .  This reading is highly uncertain, 
but the upper remains of a lamed appear in approximately the expected place for F’s proposed תלחד, and 
the other ink traces do not contradict such a reading.  The word ימע is not implausible at the beginning 
of the line. 
 161 
19.23: ֯ ש֯ ו ֯ נ ֯ א ֯ר֯ב ] מח [ ןי ֯ נ ֯ ש ̇ ש ]  J/GMT/AW ] ינש שמח שנא [ ן ; B1 ֯ ן ֯ ע֯ צ ֯ ו ֯ ע֯ר ֯ פ ֯ י ֯ד ֯ ש֯ נ ֯ א; F ] שמח ןמת תבתיו שונא רב
 ןינש [ .  J/GMT/AW’s suggestion is too short to fill the available space, while F’s is much too long.  B1’s 
reading does not fit the ink remains, some of which are visible on BZ19B.  These remains generally fit 
the letters and spacing suggested here, although the spacing would have to be compact. 
19.23: ףוסלו Qim1/GMT/F/AW ]  AY/J/B1 רתבלו.  This mistake of the earlier readings was first noted by 
Qimron and is quite obvious on the photographs. 
19.24: ◌◌◌◌◌ ◌ ̇ ל ◌◌ ל ֯ י ̇א ̇ ת̇ ל ̇ ת̇ ו  ]  J ] ותא [ תתלת ; B1 ]    [ ֯ א ֯ תל ֯ ת ; GMT/AW ] ... ותא [ תתלת ; F ] ותא [ ̇ ת ̇ ת̇ לת ̇יל ;  Pu 
had already noticed the lamed preceding אתלתו, apparent even on the plates in AY, but this observation 
went unheeded by all but F.  Furthermore, the space before this word is far too large to read simply ותא.  
The line may, however, begin with this word, since what remains of the first letter may be interpreted as 
an aleph.  The upper portion of the aleph in אתלתו is apparent in BZ19B (despite F’s assurances to the 
contrary), as is the vav at the beginning of this word.  Mu1 also reads אתלת. 
19.24: ◌◌◌ ̇ פ̇ב ̇ ע֯ר ] ו [ ]  AY/J/B1/GMT/F/AW ̇ ע̇ר ̇ פ יד ] ו [ .  In BZ19B it appears to me that a bet precedes the 
possible word וערפ, and that the previous word is not יד, since a horizontal, bottom stroke can be clearly 
seen as part of the last letter.  It may be that others have read my [ י ̇ ה֯ ו ( the left leg of the heh is clear in 
BZ19B) as a יד, which it resembles.  B1’s foregoing transcription ֯ א ֯ ת֯ י ֯ב ֯ י ֯ נ ֯ב ֯ ן ֯ מ is not plausible. 
19.24: יתמכ ̇ ח ]  AY/J/B1/GMT/F/AW יתתנא.  This reading is amazingly plain on BZ19B, although it appears 
more obscured (but still discernible) on the plates of AY.  Here is an instance where a mistaken reading 
(without any critical marks!) has been passed along for some time without being noticed. 
19.25: שו [ ן ̇ ו ֯ הל ̇ ול ֯ א ]  J/GMT/AW ] ועבו [ ל ] י [ ל ] אעדוא [ ; B1 ֯ יל ֯ ול ֯ א ֯ ש֯ ו; F ] אשו [ ל ול ] י [ .  J/GMT/AW’s 
reconstruction is much too long, since there are only three letters at most between the second lamed and 
the next word.  The vav/yod and final nun are clear following this lamed on BZ19B, assuring that this 
word is ןוהל, and not יל.  The first lamed is directly preceded by another letter, the remains of which fit an 
aleph, supporting the suggestion of B1. 
19.25: ̇ פ ̇ ס ̇ר א ]  AY/J/GMT/AW ̇ ט ̇ב ̇ ת א ; B1/F ֯ ע֯ד֯ נ ֯ מ ֯א .  I am indebted to M. Berstein (with E. Eshel) for this 
reading.  I first read אדבכ, but when the first letter is compared to the samekh of ףוסלו in 19.23 the 
similarity of the sloping, righthand stroke and the protrusion at the upper, lefthand corner are clear and 
decisive. The peh is the least definite letter paleographically speaking and could also be read as bet, since 
the critical top portion is somewhat obscured.  This would result in the equally plausible א̇ר̇ב ̇ ס, 
“brilliance, understanding.” Either word makes good sense in the present context.  The resh is sure in 
BZ19BM and BZ19B, rendering all earlier proposals untenable.  Based on the context, I take ארפס as a 
reference to “book learning, scribal wisdom, erudition” (safrah or saparah), rather than an actual book 
(sifra).  This meaning is also found in the Syriac  (sefro). 
19.25: ֯ סל ֯ר ֯ פ ̇ילמ ̇ נ ֯ ח ̇ ו ך Qim1/F ]  AY ל ]     [ ילמ ]   [ ךא ; J/GMT/AW ל ] בתכ [ ילמ ךונח ; B1 ֯ נל ◌◌ ֯ ילמ ֯ ן ֯ י ֯ נ ֯ א .  I am not 
nearly as convinced as Qim1 that J/GMT/AW’s ל ] בתכ [ does not fit the ink traces, since large parts of 
each of these letters are effaced, especially the area where the bottom of the bet would be.  Nevertheless, 
his reading also fits the remains, and I follow him here.  The word ך̇ ו ̇ נ ֯ ח is reasonably certain. 
19.26: אנט֯ב֯ב ]  AY/J/GMT/AW אנ ̇ פ̇כ̇ב.  The third letter is plainly not a peh, but a tet, as may be seen when the 
size and contrast of BZ19B are enhanced.  Both letters preceding the tet have horizontal base strokes 
characteristic of a bet or similar letter.  This noun has the advantage of making sense with the following 
הבר ̇ ת֯ א (the first letter of which is very uncertain). 
19.26: םקמל ן ̇י ֯ ת֯ א א֯ ו ֯ ו ֯ ה ]  AY ]      [ םקמל ןותאו ; J/GMT/AW ]          [ םקמל ןי ; Pu םקמל ןישנא ןותא; B1  ֯ א֯ ו ֯ ו ֯ ה
 ] עב [ םקמל ןי ; F ]       [ םקמל ןיתאו .  The first word of this phrase is uncertain, but the blurred letters do fit 
B1’s אווה quite nicely.  The second word is more sure but may either represent the peal 3 m. pl. perfect 
(ןותא) or pl. participle (ןיתא) of יתא.  I have taken it as the latter, although it must be translated 
idiomatically (e.g. “they were not about to…”).  The graphic reading of the final word is certain, but it 
has been taken to mean different things.  AY translate it as the noun for “place” (= Hebrew םוקמ), 
while most others take it to be an infinitive from םוק or םמק.  The latter makes better sense here and is 
found again in 20.20. 
 162 
19.26: חצ ̇ ה̇ עא ןוהל  ]  AY ]     [ ̇ ה ֯ הל ̇ צ ; J ◌◌◌◌ ל ם ◌◌ ; B1 ֯ ןוהל ֯ ה ֯ ת֯ י ֯ ז ֯ ח ֯ א; Pu/GMT/AW  ... ; F ]      [ ̇ ןוהל ץ .  This 
entire phrase is marvelously clear and intact in BZ19BM and BZ19B.  The meaning, however, is more 
obscure.  The first word must be a 1 sg. imperfect verb, which I take to be from the root העי / א .  This 
verb typically means “to bubble up, flow forth,” but can also be used of speech, i.e. “to utter, expound.”  
This is especially true in the aphel.  The second word typically means “brilliant, shining, clear” as an 
adjective, but is used once in the Isaiah to refer to clarity of speech (Is. 32:4; תוחצ רבדל).  Hence, I 
tentatively take this as a reference to the purity of teaching given by Abram.  One should note that AW 
consistently transliterates what are intended to be ellipses in GMT as three, undiscernible letters. 
Column 20:  This column is the first whose text is preserved nearly in its entirety, although a few lines at the 
top are obscured by decay.  For this and the following columns the BZ photos generally portray the 
scroll in worse condition than the AY plates and certain of the IMneg. photographs.  Despite this, there 
are isolated cases where the BZ set provides clear evidence against previous readings. 
20.2: ֯ ח֯ צ֯ י ֯ נ ]  J ◌◌ צ ◌ ; B1 ֯ םל ֯ ש; GMT/AW  ... ; F צנ ] י [ ח .  Judging from the plates of AY (which are much better 
than the others in this area) there is no room for another letter between the tsade and het, while the 
bottom tip of a yod/vav can be discerned before both letters.  Indeed, the expected (plene) form would 
have a yod in the second position, not the third as in F (cf. Jastrow II, p. 928).  B1’s transcription is not 
plausible. 
20.3: ֯ צ֯ י ֯ מ ֯ ם֯ י ֯ ע֯ נ ] הח [ ֯ א ] ו [ ̇ק̇י ̇ קר ]  J ] נ [ קיקר אמו םיע ; B1 ] א [ ֯ץ֯ י ֯ קו ֯ יג ֯ ש ֯ ם֯ ו ֯כ ; GMT/AW ] נ [ קיקר אמכו םיע ; F  םיענ
 ] ו [ קיקר .  The readings of J and F do not posit enough letters to fit the available space and ink remains 
and must be incorrect.  When BZ20T is enlarged, and the contrast enhanced, the remains of a mem and 
tsade can be recognized, leading to my proposed reading, and rendering B1’s suggestion improbable (the 
word קיקר “soft” was first suggested by Kutscher).  My reading requires the het and heh to be spaced 
compactly and so remains uncertain.  I am quite convinced, however, of the presence of some form of 
the word חצמ “forehead” for the second word of the line.  The first word of the line, and the vav 
preceding קיקר, are very uncertain. 
20.4: ֯ר̇י ̇ פ ̇ ש֯ מ ]  AY/J/GMT/F/AW ]   [ ; Pu ץיצנ; B1 ֯ר ֯ א ֯ מ ] ך [ .  BZ20T shows quite convincingly the letter 
combination shin-peh-yod/vav in the middle of this word, leading to my proposal.  The most certain of 
these letters is the peh, leaving the suggestions of B1 and Pu doubtful.  If correct, this word appears to be 
a m. sg. pael part. paired with the preceding noun chain אהיפנא ץנ (although the initial letter may also be 
a kaph; i.e. ֯ר̇י ̇ פ ̇ ש֯כ).  F’s question (p. 194) “Is there room for all that?” may be answered affirmatively. 
20.4: אהיערד AY/J/B1/GMT/F ]  AW ד ד אהיער .  This appears to be a case of dittography by AW. 
20.5: ןליל֯כ AY/J/GMT/AW/F ]  B1 ֯ד ןליל .  The bottom stroke of the first letter can be seen below the lamed in 
BZ20T and IMneg. 3859. 
20.5: ד֯ י ֯ מ ̇ חו לוכ  F/GMT/AW ]  AY ו ]    [ לוכ ; J  אמו ◌ ◌ ל ; Pu לוכ ריחבו; B1 לוכ ך֯ ז ֯ א ֯ מו.  F’s reading דימחו was first 
suggested by Michaud, and fits the letter remains fairly well.  The traces of the first two letters do not 
support the suggestion of Puech (especially the second, which appears to have a semi-horizontal base 
stroke), and the final dalet of this word extends no farther down than the surrounding letters (contra B1).  
J’s proposal is too short. 
20.5: אהיפכ J/B1/Mu2/GMT/AW/F ]  AY היפכ.  The final aleph is obvious in AY’s plates. 
20.7: ̇ ת̇רפש B1/Qim1 ]  AY/J/GMT/F/AW ̇ ה̇רפש.  Once scrutinized, it is quite clear that the final letter is a 
tav that has had its lower, left leg effaced (the upper, left leg and joint are the key indicators). 
20.7: אהידילדו Ros/J/GMT/F/AW ]  AY/Gin/B1 לדו אהידי .  The letters are undisputed, but there has been a 
longstanding debate over whether they should be divided into two words.  If the letters are divided as in 
AY/Gin/B1, the noun לד is difficult to make sense of, while the compound preposition (dalet plus lamed) 
has disturbed other commentators.  I find the latter problem less troubling, and better fitting the context 
here.  For a fuller discussion cf. F, p. 197. 
20.17: יהו א F ] AY/J/B1/GMT/AW והו א .  F understands this to be the 3 f. sg. ind. personal pronoun, rather 
than a 3 m. sg. peal perfect verb.  His position accords better with the following המע, since others must 
 163 
either take אוהו to be a mistaken verbal form (i.e. it is meant to be the feminine תאוה; so AW?) or the 
suffix of המע to be feminine, despite its typical morphology (אה-) in the scroll. 
20.22: ֯ ז ̇ ח ]    ינ [ ]  J/GMT/F/AW ̇ ז ̇ ח ] ינ [ ; B1 זח ] ןכ א [ .  Even the plate in AY reveals that ינזח alone does not 
account for the available space.  B1’s suggestion is more acceptable with regard to space, but still falls 
approximately one letter short. 
20.25: ֯ י וב̇י ̇ ת AY/Gin/J/GMT/F/AW ] B1 ובי ֯ ת֯ א.  The slight ink remains visible on BZ20M and IMneg. 3859 
do not allow a decisive judgment regarding B1’s proposed aleph.  The first letter is almost completely 
effaced, and his reading remains possible, but the yod of an imperf. form would better fit the expected 
syntax and morphology.

belief that this word is continued on the following line – something which happens nowhere else in the

have incorporated two distinct readings from variant editions of the text – one which read לע and the 
other יהולע – to begin the phrase!  There are definitely not two occurences of לע here.

20.32: ֯ י ֯ קפני ] ירצמ ןמ [ ֯ ן ]  AY ֯ קפני ] ; J קפני ]       יננו [ ; B1  ֯ ן ֯ מ ֯ י ֯ נ ֯ נ֯ ו ֯ קפני ] ג [ ֯ א ֯ ו ] ר [ ן ֯ י ֯ר֯ צ ֯ מ ֯ ע ; F ̇ קפני ]     ןירצמ ןמ יננו [ ;

ןירצמ, is grossly inaccurate with regard to available space, and also does not take due account of the 
lamed less than halfway between פני ֯ ק ... and the end of the line. 
20.33: תלבגו ]  AY/F ̇ זאו תל ; J/B1/GMT/AW זאו תל .  What is perceptible with difficulty on AY’s plate is starkly 
obvious on BZ20B.  The second and third letters are very clearly gimel-bet, not aleph-zayin (the bottom of 
the bet is also easily seen on IMneg. 3859).  The typical Aramaic meanings of this verb are “knead, create, 
grow in size [used only of parasites]” (Jastrow I, 207; Sokoloff, p. 119).  While the last meaning must be 
the general sense in which the word is used here, this attestation represents a novel usage and so adds to 
our knowledge of the Aramaic lexicon at this time.  Context dictates the meaning to be something such 
as “I grew, became wealthy,” – a meaning which seems distantly related to the nominative meaning 
“border, outer limits” (i.e. the limits of Abram’s possessions were affected). 
20.33: ] זאו [ ̇ ל ] טול [ F ]  AY/GMT/AW ] טולו [ ; J ] טול לזאו [ ; B1 ] ו [ ל ] טו [ .  The best view of the lamed is found on 
AY’s plate, which shows only the negative imprint where the ink has eaten away the leather.  This 
imprint looks too far away from the nun of ןירצמ (approx. 2-3 letters) to have a vav alone intervening.

making a heh likely.  The variant spelling ארש is, however, found in 22.13. 
Column 21:  Only a small portion of the bottom of this column is missing.  The text is otherwise in excellent 
condition compared to the rest of the scroll. 
21.1: ̇כ ל ]  AY/GMT/F/AW ] ב [ ל ̇כ ; Ros/Qim1/B1 לע; J לכב.  The split in the leather at the inscribed margin 
line appears to be quite clean, and I am unconvinced that an entire letter has been lost.  J certainly did 
not see an intact bet when viewing the photograph and should have placed this letter in brackets.  The 
letter preceding the lamed is unlikely to be an ayin judging from the length of the stroke still visible, which 
is not intersected by another line.  If two strokes did intersect above what is currently visible, the space 
between letters would be rather large.  Qim1 is undecided on whether this letter is an ayin or kaph but 
agrees that there was no letter preceding it.  The only other defective spelling of לוכ is in 20.6. 
21.2: ̇ ל ◌ תברק̇ ו  ]  AY/J/GMT/AW ] ו [ ̇ א תברק ; B1 תברק֯ ו; F ̇ א̇ ו תברק .  It is puzzling that no previous editions

letter can be seen in both AY’s plate and BZ20B.  It appears that the lamed was followed by a small letter 
and then the word תברקו.  The lamed may also have been preceded by another letter.  Which word stood 
here is difficult to surmise, but the clear physical evidence should not be disregarded.  Perhaps it is the 
word יל, “for myself”?

21.10: יתרחמל Gin/J/B1/GMT/F/AW ]  AY תרחמל ו .  For the linguistic reasoning behind this change see

21.23: לערת VdK/B1 ]  AY/J/GMT/F/AW דת לע .  One could not ask for a clearer resh than in this word (cf.

and related forms are attested in the LXX (Qarga&l) and Jub. 13:22 (Tergal). 
21.24: איה B1/F ] AY/J/GMT/AW וה א .  The transcription of this word determines to which referent it

21.26: אדמ Kut/Gin/J/B1/GMT/F/AW ]  AY רמ א .  This is a misprint in AY. 
21.30: ֯ד ֯ ן ֯ י ֯ על ]           אני [ ◌ ֯ י ֯ד  ]  AY ]    [ ןיל ]                    [ ; J/Qim1(?)  ןיעל ]             אניד [ ; B1  ֯ א֯ נ֯ י ֯ד ֯ ן ֯ י ֯ על
